the other team is the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> (owned by Canadian media conglomerate  <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Communications" title="Rogers Communications">Rogers Communications</a>).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007:_More_struggles">2007: More struggles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2007: More struggles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2007 Atlanta Braves season">2007 Atlanta Braves season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BrianMcCann.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/BrianMcCann.JPG/170px-BrianMcCann.JPG" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/BrianMcCann.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="183" data-file-height="279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BrianMcCann.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brian_McCann_(baseball)" title="Brian McCann (baseball)">Brian McCann</a> bats for Atlanta in July 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>On July 5, <a href="/wiki/Chipper_Jones" title="Chipper Jones">Chipper Jones</a> surpassed Dale Murphy for the Atlanta club record of 372 home runs by belting two against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>.\n</p><p>After struggling during the second half of the 2007 season, Atlanta finished over .500 and missed the post season again. On October 12, 2007, <a href="/wiki/John_Schuerholz" title="John Schuerholz">John Schuerholz</a> stepped down as General Manager to take over as team president.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Assistant GM <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wren" title="Frank Wren">Frank Wren</a> took over as General Manager.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009:_The_return_of_solid_pitching">2009: The return of solid pitching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2009: The return of solid pitching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2009_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2009 Atlanta Braves season">2009 Atlanta Braves season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3,_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg" width="220" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3%2C_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1713" data-file-height="1540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenshin_Kawakami_on_August_3,_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kenshin_Kawakami" title="Kenshin Kawakami">Kenshin Kawakami</a> pitching for the Braves in 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>On December 4, 2008, the Atlanta Braves received <a href="/wiki/Javier_V%C3%A1zquez" title="Javier V\xc3\xa1zquez">Javier V\xc3\xa1zquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boone_Logan" title="Boone Logan">Boone Logan</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> received prospects catcher <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Flowers" title="Tyler Flowers">Tyler Flowers</a>, shortstop <a href="/wiki/Brent_Lillibridge" title="Brent Lillibridge">Brent Lillibridge</a>, third baseman <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jon_Gilmore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jon Gilmore (page does not exist)">Jon Gilmore</a> and pitcher <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santos_Rodriguez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santos Rodriguez (page does not exist)">Santos Rodriguez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  On January 13, 2009, the Braves signed Japanese pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kenshin_Kawakami" title="Kenshin Kawakami">Kenshin Kawakami</a> to a three-year deal, and two days later signed free agent pitcher <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lowe" title="Derek Lowe">Derek Lowe</a> to a four-year contract. During the course of the offseason, the Braves signed veteran pitcher and former Brave <a href="/wiki/Tom_Glavine" title="Tom Glavine">Tom Glavine</a>, while losing long-time Brave <a href="/wiki/John_Smoltz" title="John Smoltz">John Smoltz</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>.\n</p><p>On February 25, 2009, just before the start of spring training, Atlanta agreed to terms on a one-year contract with free-agent outfielder <a href="/wiki/Garret_Anderson" title="Garret Anderson">Garret Anderson</a>. The additional outfield depth allowed the Braves to trade <a href="/wiki/Josh_Anderson_(baseball)" title="Josh Anderson (baseball)">Josh Anderson</a> to the Detroit Tigers for minor league pitcher <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rudy_Darrow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rudy Darrow (page does not exist)">Rudy Darrow</a> on March 30, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 3, 2009, the Braves acquired <a href="/wiki/Nate_McLouth" title="Nate McLouth">Nate McLouth</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> for prospects <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Locke_(baseball)" title="Jeff Locke (baseball)">Jeff Locke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Morton_(pitcher)" title="Charlie Morton (pitcher)">Charlie Morton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gorkys_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Gorkys Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Gorkys Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>. They also released veteran pitcher Tom Glavine. On July 10, 2009, the Braves traded outfielder <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Francoeur" title="Jeff Francoeur">Jeff Francoeur</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> for outfielder <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Church" title="Ryan Church">Ryan Church</a>. On July 31, 2009, hours before the trade deadline, the Braves and Boston Red Sox swapped 1st basemen: Atlanta dealt <a href="/wiki/Casey_Kotchman" title="Casey Kotchman">Casey Kotchman</a> to Boston and reacquired <a href="/wiki/Adam_LaRoche" title="Adam LaRoche">Adam LaRoche</a>, whom the Braves had traded away during the 2006\xe2\x80\x9307 off-season to Pittsburgh.\n</p><p>The Braves made a late-season surge, coming within 2 games of the wild card leading <a href="/wiki/2009_Colorado_Rockies_season" title="2009 Colorado Rockies season">Colorado Rockies</a> in late September. On October 1, 2009 with the Braves four games back, Colorado beat the <a href="/wiki/2009_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="2009 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a> 9\xe2\x80\x932 to clinch the wild card spot and end the Braves\' 2009 postseason hopes.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2010:_Cox.27s_final_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010:_Cox\'s_final_season">2010: Cox\'s final season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2010: Cox&#039;s final season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2010 Atlanta Braves season">2010 Atlanta Braves season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg/150px-Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg" width="150" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg/225px-Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg/300px-Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="1842" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Cox_signs_autograph_CROPPED.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Braves manager <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Cox" title="Bobby Cox">Bobby Cox</a> retired in 2010 after 25 years of management</div></div></div>\n<p>The 2010 Atlanta Braves Season features the Braves\' attempt to reclaim a <a href="/wiki/Postseason" class="mw-redirect" title="Postseason">postseason</a> berth for the first time since <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2005 Atlanta Braves season">2005</a>. The Braves were once again skippered by <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Cox" title="Bobby Cox">Bobby Cox</a>, now in his 25th and final season managing the team. The Braves started the 2010 season slowly and had a nine-game losing streak in April. Then they had a nine-game winning streak from May 26 through June 3, the Braves longest since <a href="/wiki/2000_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2000 Atlanta Braves season">2000</a> when they won 16 in a row. On May 31, the Atlanta Braves defeated the then-first place <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> at <a href="/wiki/Turner_Field" title="Turner Field">Turner Field</a> to take sole possession of first place in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> standings, a position they had maintained through the middle of August.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The last time the Atlanta Braves led the NL East on August 1 was in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2005 Atlanta Braves season">2005</a>. On July 13, 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/2010_MLB_All-Star_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 MLB All-Star Game">2010 MLB All-Star Game</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim">Anaheim</a>, Braves catcher <a href="/wiki/Brian_McCann_(baseball)" title="Brian McCann (baseball)">Brian McCann</a> was awarded the <a href="/wiki/MLB_All-Star_Game_MVP_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB All-Star Game MVP Award">All-Star Game MVP Award</a> for his clutch two-out, three-run double in the seventh inning to give the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> its first win in the All-Star Game since <a href="/wiki/1996_MLB_All-Star_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="1996 MLB All-Star Game">1996</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He became the first Brave to win the All-Star Game MVP Award since <a href="/wiki/Fred_McGriff" title="Fred McGriff">Fred McGriff</a> did so in 1994. The Braves made two deals before the trade deadline to acquire <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lex_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(shortstop,_born_1977)" title="\xc3\x81lex Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (shortstop, born 1977)">\xc3\x81lex Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ankiel" title="Rick Ankiel">Rick Ankiel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Farnsworth" title="Kyle Farnsworth">Kyle Farnsworth</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>, giving up shortstop <a href="/wiki/Yunel_Escobar" title="Yunel Escobar">Yunel Escobar</a>, pitchers <a href="/wiki/Jo-Jo_Reyes" title="Jo-Jo Reyes">Jo-Jo Reyes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Chavez" title="Jesse Chavez">Jesse Chavez</a>, outfielder <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Blanco" title="Gregor Blanco">Gregor Blanco</a> and three minor leaguers.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On August 18, 2010 they traded three pitching prospects for first baseman <a href="/wiki/Derrek_Lee" title="Derrek Lee">Derrek Lee</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On August 22, 2010 against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Minor_(baseball)" title="Mike Minor (baseball)">Mike Minor</a> struck out 12 batters across 6 innings; an Atlanta Braves single game rookie strikeout record.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The Braves dropped to second in the NL East in early September, but won the NL Wild Card. They lost to the <a href="/wiki/2010_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2010 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_National_League_Division_Series" title="2010 National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> in four games. Every game of the series was determined by one run. After the series-clinching victory for the Giants in Game 4, Bobby Cox was given a standing ovation by the fans, also by players and coaches of both the Braves and Giants.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2011:_Fredi_Gonz.C3.A1lez_takes_over"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011:_Fredi_Gonz\xc3\xa1lez_takes_over">2011: Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez takes over</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2011: Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez takes over">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2011 Atlanta Braves season">2011 Atlanta Braves season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg/170px-Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg/255px-Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg/340px-Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="1562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Craig_Kimbrel_9-12-11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Braves <a href="/wiki/Closer_(baseball)" title="Closer (baseball)">closer</a> <a href="/wiki/Craig_Kimbrel" title="Craig Kimbrel">Craig Kimbrel</a> pitching in 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>On October 13, 2010, the Atlanta Braves announced that <a href="/wiki/Fredi_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez">Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> would replace long-time Braves manager <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Cox" title="Bobby Cox">Bobby Cox</a> as manager of the team in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The announcement came just two days after the <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2010 Atlanta Braves season">2010 Braves</a> were eliminated from the postseason. It was also announced that pitching coach <a href="/wiki/Roger_McDowell" title="Roger McDowell">Roger McDowell</a>, third-base coach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Snitker" title="Brian Snitker">Brian Snitker</a>, and bullpen coach <a href="/wiki/Eddie_P%C3%A9rez_(baseball)" title="Eddie P\xc3\xa9rez (baseball)">Eddie P\xc3\xa9rez</a> would retain their current positions, while former hitting coach <a href="/wiki/Terry_Pendleton" title="Terry Pendleton">Terry Pendleton</a> would replace <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hubbard_(baseball)" title="Glenn Hubbard (baseball)">Glenn Hubbard</a> as the first-base coach and newcomer <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tosca" title="Carlos Tosca">Carlos Tosca</a> would become the new bench coach. Hubbard and former bench coach <a href="/wiki/Chino_Cadahia" title="Chino Cadahia">Chino Cadahia</a> were not offered positions on the new coaching staff. <a href="/wiki/Larry_Parrish" title="Larry Parrish">Larry Parrish</a> was hired as hitting coach on October 29, 2010.\n</p><p>On November 16, 2010 in an offseason trade, the Braves acquired <a href="/wiki/Dan_Uggla" title="Dan Uggla">Dan Uggla</a> from the Florida Marlins in exchange for left-handed reliever <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dunn_(baseball)" title="Mike Dunn (baseball)">Mike Dunn</a> and infielder <a href="/wiki/Omar_Infante" title="Omar Infante">Omar Infante</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Elias_Sports_Bureau" title="Elias Sports Bureau">Elias Sports Bureau</a>, the Braves had an all-time franchise win-loss record over .500 for the first time since 1923 after their win over the <a href="/wiki/2011_Houston_Astros_season" title="2011 Houston Astros season">Houston Astros</a> on June 11, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Braves franchise became the third franchise in MLB history to reach 10,000 wins with their win over the <a href="/wiki/2011_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2011 Washington Nationals season">Washington Nationals</a> on July 15, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On July 31, 2011, just sixteen days after registering their 10,000th win, the <a href="/wiki/2011_Florida_Marlins_season" title="2011 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a> defeated the Braves by a score of 3\xe2\x80\x931, handing the team the 10,000th loss in franchise history. The Braves become only the second team in big league history with 10,000 losses after the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> reached the plateau in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Players from the Braves\' farm system, such as <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Freeman" title="Freddie Freeman">Freddie Freeman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Beachy" title="Brandon Beachy">Brandon Beachy</a>, played regularly with the big league club, while <a href="/wiki/Julio_Teher%C3%A1n" title="Julio Teher\xc3\xa1n">Julio Teher\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randall_Delgado" title="Randall Delgado">Randall Delgado</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Minor_(baseball)" title="Mike Minor (baseball)">Mike Minor</a> were called up for spot starts. With late season injuries to starters <a href="/wiki/Jair_Jurrjens" title="Jair Jurrjens">Jair Jurrjens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hanson" title="Tommy Hanson">Tommy Hanson</a>, these three young pitchers made their way into the starting rotation in their absence.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Eight players made their major league debuts for the team in 2011.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="September_collapse">September collapse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: September collapse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>The Braves led the <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_Wild_Card_winners" title="List of National League Wild Card winners">National League Wild Card</a> standings for much of the 2011 season, with the division-rival <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> firmly in control of first place in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a>. The Braves entered the final month of the regular season 25 games above .500 with a record of 80\xe2\x80\x9355 and an &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap">8<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span>-game lead in the Wild Card standings. The nearest team trailing them, the <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, who also trailed the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">National League Central</a>-leading <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> by &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap">8<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span> games at the time, were considered a long-shot to gain a spot in the postseason. Just days prior on August 26, the Cardinals found themselves &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap">10<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span> games behind and in third place.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With 27 games to play, the Braves went 9\xe2\x80\x9318 in September to finish the season with a record of 89\xe2\x80\x9373. The Cardinals, meanwhile, went 18\xe2\x80\x938 to finish at 90\xe2\x80\x9372. Braves closer <a href="/wiki/Craig_Kimbrel" title="Craig Kimbrel">Craig Kimbrel</a>, who had not surrendered a single earned run in July or August, carried a 4.76 ERA in September with three blown saves. After being dominant in his role for much of the season, Braves setup man <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Venters" title="Jonny Venters">Jonny Venters</a> posted a 5.11 September ERA. These sharp declines in both relievers led many critics to question the handling of the bullpen by Braves manager <a href="/wiki/Fredi_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez">Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Veteran starter <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lowe" title="Derek Lowe">Derek Lowe</a> posted a <a href="/wiki/Win-loss_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Win-loss record">win-loss record</a> of 0\xe2\x80\x935 in September with an ERA of 8.75.<sup id="cite_ref-AJC_chronology_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJC_chronology-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Shortly into the offseason, Lowe would be traded to the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Braves starters lasted six or more innings only three times over the last 23 games.<sup id="cite_ref-AJC_chronology_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJC_chronology-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Over the last five games, all of which were losses for the Braves, the team managed to score only seven runs.<sup id="cite_ref-collapse_complete_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collapse_complete-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Braves catcher <a href="/wiki/Brian_McCann_(baseball)" title="Brian McCann (baseball)">Brian McCann</a>, often regarded as the best offensive catcher in the Majors, hit only .183 with two home runs in September.<sup id="cite_ref-AJC_chronology_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJC_chronology-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The offense as a whole hit for only a .235 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average_(baseball)" title="Batting average (baseball)">batting average</a> and a .300 <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a> in September, both second-worst in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>. The .195 <a href="/wiki/Scoring_position" title="Scoring position">RISP</a> average by Braves hitters was second worst in the Majors.<sup id="cite_ref-AJC_chronology_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJC_chronology-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Hitting coach <a href="/wiki/Larry_Parrish" title="Larry Parrish">Larry Parrish</a> was fired two days following the last game of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2012:_Chipper.27s_last_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012:_Chipper\'s_last_season">2012: Chipper\'s last season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2012: Chipper&#039;s last season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg/170px-Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg" width="170" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg/255px-Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg/340px-Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg 2x" data-file-width="356" data-file-height="595" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipper_Jones_last_reg_season_game.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chipper Jones salutes the crowd at <a href="/wiki/Turner_Field" title="Turner Field">Turner Field</a> prior to his final regular season game on September 30, 2012. Jones announced he would retire after 19 seasons with the Braves</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2012, the Braves began their 138th season after an upsetting end to the 2011 season. On March 22, the Braves announced that third baseman <a href="/wiki/Chipper_Jones" title="Chipper Jones">Chipper Jones</a> would retire following the 2012 season after 19 Major League seasons with the team. The Braves also lost many key players through trades or free agency, including pitcher <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lowe" title="Derek Lowe">Derek Lowe</a>, shortstop <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lex_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(shortstop,_born_1977)" title="\xc3\x81lex Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (shortstop, born 1977)">Alex Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>, and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Nate_McLouth" title="Nate McLouth">Nate McLouth</a>. To compensate for this, the team went on to receive many key players such as outfielder <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bourn" title="Michael Bourn">Michael Bourn</a>, along with shortstops <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Pastornicky" title="Tyler Pastornicky">Tyler Pastornicky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrelton_Simmons" title="Andrelton Simmons">Andrelton Simmons</a>. To fill the void of a quality starting pitcher left by Lowe (as well as a mid-season injury to <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Beachy" title="Brandon Beachy">Brandon Beachy</a>), manager Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez elected relief pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kris_Medlen" title="Kris Medlen">Kris Medlen</a> to the starting pitching rotation. The Braves went on to win every game Medlen started, setting the MLB record for most consecutive wins when a single pitcher starts (total of 23). Atlanta stayed close to the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> in the race to win the National League East title. They also stayed on top of the National League Wild Card race. Washington ended up winning their first division title in franchise history, but the Braves remained in first place of the NL wild card race. Keeping with a new MLB rule for the 2012 season, the top two wild card teams in each league must play each other in a <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2012 National League Wild Card Game">playoff game</a> before entering into the <a href="/wiki/Division_Series" title="Division Series">Division Series</a>.\n</p><p>The Braves played the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in the first ever <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Wild_Card_Game" title="Major League Baseball Wild Card Game">Wild Card Game</a>. The Braves were behind 6\xe2\x80\x933 in the bottom of the eighth inning when Andrelton Simmons hit a fly ball to left field that dropped in between the Cardinals shortstop and left fielder. Umpire <a href="/wiki/Sam_Holbrook" title="Sam Holbrook">Sam Holbrook</a> called Simmons out, citing the <a href="/wiki/Infield_fly_rule" title="Infield fly rule">infield fly rule</a>. Had an infield fly not been called, Simmons would have been credited with a single and Atlanta would have had the bases loaded with one out. Fans at Turner Field began to litter the field with debris, prompting the game to be delayed for 19 minutes. The Braves lost the game 6\xe2\x80\x933, ending their season.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013:_Braves_win_the_East">2013: Braves win the East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2013: Braves win the East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2013 Atlanta Braves season">2013 Atlanta Braves season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Evan_Gattis_on_April_7,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg/220px-Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg/330px-Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg/440px-Evan_Gattis_on_April_7%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Evan_Gattis_on_April_7,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Evan_Gattis" title="Evan Gattis">Evan Gattis</a> catching for the Braves in 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>During the offseason following a gut wrenching exit against the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Wild_Card_Game" title="Major League Baseball Wild Card Game">Wild Card Game</a>, the Braves spent the 2012\xe2\x80\x932013 offseason revamping and retooling their offense. The Braves turned heads across baseball by acquiring <a href="/wiki/B.J._Upton" class="mw-redirect" title="B.J. Upton">B.J. Upton</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a>, signing him to a 5-year $75.25 million contract and making him their starting center fielder,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and uniting him with his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Justin_Upton" title="Justin Upton">Justin Upton</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> in a seven player trade that sent fan favorite utility man <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Prado" title="Mart\xc3\xadn Prado">Mart\xc3\xadn Prado</a> to the Diamondbacks,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> they also filled a need for a new Third Baseman in <a href="/wiki/Chris_Johnson_(baseball)" title="Chris Johnson (baseball)">Chris Johnson</a> after the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Chipper_Jones" title="Chipper Jones">Chipper Jones</a> the previous year. The Braves began the 2013 season with a hot start in April by going 17\xe2\x80\x939 for the month, which saw the emergence of rookie sensation <a href="/wiki/Evan_Gattis" title="Evan Gattis">Evan Gattis</a>, while taking hold of first place in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> division, a lead they would never relinquish for the rest of the season. The Braves suffered many injuries to key players throughout the season, including injuries to <a href="/wiki/Jason_Heyward" title="Jason Heyward">Jason Heyward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_McCann_(baseball)" title="Brian McCann (baseball)">Brian McCann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Freeman" title="Freddie Freeman">Freddie Freeman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_O%27Flaherty" title="Eric O&#39;Flaherty">Eric O\'Flaherty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Venters" title="Jonny Venters">Jonny Venters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_Pena" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramiro Pena">Ramiro Pena</a> and others, but found a way to win despite these blows to the team. Leading up to the All Star break, First Baseman Freddie Freeman was voted in to play for the 2013 National League All-Star Team, in the 2013 All Star Game, which he did not play. The Braves also witnessed the emergence of rookie pitcher <a href="/wiki/Julio_Teher%C3%A1n" title="Julio Teher\xc3\xa1n">Julio Teher\xc3\xa1n</a> after much hype during Spring training. From July 26 to August 10, the Braves won 14 games in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  The winning streak was the longest of its kind since April\xe2\x80\x93May 2000.\n</p><p>On June 28, 2013 the Atlanta Braves retired former third baseman Chipper Jones\' jersey, number 10, before the game against the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>. He was honored before 51,300 fans at <a href="/wiki/Turner_Field" title="Turner Field">Turner Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He served as a staple of the Braves franchise for 19 years before announcing his retirement at the beginning of the 2012 season. <a href="/wiki/Chipper_Jones" title="Chipper Jones">Chipper Jones</a> played his last regular season game for the Braves on September 30, 2012.\n</p><p>The Braves opened up a 15-game lead on the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> on September 3, 2013, riding that lead en route to its first division title since 2005, the last of 14 straight division titles. This was also Braves manager <a href="/wiki/Fredi_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez">Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>\'s first division title since beginning his managerial career in 1990; including his first since becoming the manager of the Braves after the 2010 season. The Braves clinched the 18th division title in team history on September 22, 2013<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> after a Nationals loss to the Marlins in the first game of a double header; the Braves also won their game that day, beating the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> 5\xe2\x80\x932 at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>.\n</p><p>After clinching the division title, they lost to the Dodgers 3\xe2\x80\x931 in the Division Series.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014:_Losing_season">2014: Losing season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2014: Losing season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heywardb2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Heywardb2014.jpg/220px-Heywardb2014.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Heywardb2014.jpg/330px-Heywardb2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Heywardb2014.jpg/440px-Heywardb2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1560" data-file-height="1974" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heywardb2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jason_Heyward" title="Jason Heyward">Jason Heyward</a> runs the bases in 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>On November 11, 2013, the Braves announced that they would vacate Turner Field for a <a href="/wiki/SunTrust_Park" title="SunTrust Park">new stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cobb_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Cobb County">Cobb County</a>, in the northwest suburbs outside of Atlanta in 2017. The move is to follow the expiration of the Braves\' 20-year lease on Turner Field in 2016. The new stadium is to be constructed in a public/private partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  During the offseason the Braves signed few of their young talents to multi year contracts; Craig Kimbrel (4 years/$42M), Freddie Freeman (8 years/$135M), Kris Medlen (1 year/$5.8M), Jason Heyward (2 years/$13.3M), Julio Teher\xc3\xa1n (6 years/$32.4M) and Andrelton Simmons (7 years/$58M).\n</p><p>The Braves finished the season in a distant second place with a 79\xe2\x80\x9383 record, which was their first losing season since 2008 and only their third since 1990.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.932016:_Rebuilding"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015\xe2\x80\x932016:_Rebuilding">2015\xe2\x80\x932016: Rebuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2015\xe2\x80\x932016: Rebuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Prior to the 2015 season, the Braves fired their General Manager <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wren" title="Frank Wren">Frank Wren</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Hart_(baseball)" title="John Hart (baseball)">John Hart</a> replaced him as interim general manager, choosing to only take the title of President of Baseball Operations. The Braves promptly traded <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Jason_Heyward" title="Jason Heyward">Jason Heyward</a> to the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> along with pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Walden" title="Jordan Walden">Jordan Walden</a> for pitchers <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Miller" title="Shelby Miller">Shelby Miller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyrell_Jenkins" title="Tyrell Jenkins">Tyrell Jenkins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Hart would then trade All Star left fielder <a href="/wiki/Justin_Upton" title="Justin Upton">Justin Upton</a> to the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> for <a href="/wiki/Max_Fried" title="Max Fried">Max Fried</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jace_Peterson" title="Jace Peterson">Jace Peterson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Peterson" title="Dustin Peterson">Dustin Peterson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mallex_Smith" title="Mallex Smith">Mallex Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Catcher <a href="/wiki/Evan_Gattis" title="Evan Gattis">Evan Gattis</a> and minor league <a href="/wiki/Prospect_(sports)" title="Prospect (sports)">prospect</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Hoyt_(baseball)" title="James Hoyt (baseball)">James Hoyt</a> were traded to the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> for minor leaguers <a href="/wiki/Mike_Foltynewicz" title="Mike Foltynewicz">Mike Foltynewicz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ruiz" title="Rio Ruiz">Rio Ruiz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Thurman" title="Andrew Thurman">Andrew Thurman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> A day before the season began, the Braves made a final trade involving former All- Star <a href="/wiki/Craig_Kimbrel" title="Craig Kimbrel">Craig Kimbrel</a> and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Melvin_Upton_Jr." title="Melvin Upton Jr.">Melvin Upton Jr.</a>. They were traded to the San Diego Padres for outfielders <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Maybin" title="Cameron Maybin">Cameron Maybin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Quentin" title="Carlos Quentin">Carlos Quentin</a> along with two minor league players.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> By the beginning of the season, the Braves did 11 trades in all.\n</p><p>Prior to the start of the 2016 regular season, the Braves continued their offseason rebuilding by trading <a href="/wiki/Andrelton_Simmons" title="Andrelton Simmons">Andrelton Simmons</a> to the Los Angeles Angels for <a href="/wiki/Erick_Aybar" title="Erick Aybar">Erick Aybar</a>, and pitching prospects <a href="/wiki/Sean_Newcomb" title="Sean Newcomb">Sean Newcomb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Ellis_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Ellis (baseball)">Chris Ellis</a> and $2.5 million. They agreed to 1 year contracts with <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Johnson_(baseball)" title="Kelly Johnson (baseball)">Kelly Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Withrow" title="Chris Withrow">Chris Withrow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arodys_Vizcaino" class="mw-redirect" title="Arodys Vizcaino">Arodys Vizcaino</a>, and agreed to terms on a minor league contract for <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Torres_(pitcher)" title="Carlos Torres (pitcher)">Carlos Torres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Francoeur" title="Jeff Francoeur">Jeff Francoeur</a>. The Braves would end up purchasing the Major League contract of Francoeur.\n</p><p>On April 13, 2016, Hector Olivera was arrested and charged with the assault of a woman at the team hotel when the Braves were in Washington D.C. facing the Nationals. He was placed on Administrative Leave by Major League Baseball and was placed on the Braves Restricted List until further disciplinary action is given.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Braves began the season on a nine-game losing streak, which is the worst opening by the franchise since 1988, when they dropped the first 10 games of that season.\n</p><p>After a 9\xe2\x80\x9328 start in 2016, Fredi Gonz\xc3\xa1lez was fired on May 17 and replaced by third base coach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Snitker" title="Brian Snitker">Brian Snitker</a> as interim general manager. Snitker replaced Gonz\xc3\xa1lez once before in the 2006\xe2\x80\x9307 off-season as the Braves third base coach when Gonz\xc3\xa1lez left the Braves to manage the Marlins.  The Braves finished the season 68\xe2\x80\x9393 and in last place in NL East.\n</p><p>During the 2016 off-season, the Braves signed pitchers <a href="/wiki/R.A._Dickey" title="R.A. Dickey">R.A. Dickey</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bartolo_Col%C3%B3n" title="Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n">Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n</a><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and promoted interim manager Brian Snitker to full-time manager.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017:_SunTrust_Park_and_front_office_changes">2017: SunTrust Park and front office changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2017: SunTrust Park and front office changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg/300px-SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg/450px-SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg/600px-SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SunTrust_Park_Opening_Day_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/SunTrust_Park" title="SunTrust Park">SunTrust Park</a> prior to its first regular-season game</div></div></div>\n<p>The Braves opened their new stadium, <a href="/wiki/SunTrust_Park" title="SunTrust Park">SunTrust Park</a>, on April 14, 2017, with a four-game sweep of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>. The park received positive reviews. Woody Studenmund of the <a href="/wiki/Hardball_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardball Times">Hardball Times</a> called the park a "gem" and he was impressed with "the compact beauty of the stadium and its exciting approach to combining baseball, business and social activities."<sup id="cite_ref-htreview_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-htreview-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  J.J. Cooper of <a href="/wiki/Baseball_America" title="Baseball America">Baseball America</a> praised the "excellent sight lines for pretty much every seat."<sup id="cite_ref-bareview_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bareview-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Cooper also noted that "the Wi-Fi works and it\'s very fast, even with a park full of smartphone users."<sup id="cite_ref-bareview_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bareview-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 2, 2017, <a href="/wiki/John_Coppolella" title="John Coppolella">John Coppolella</a> resigned as general manager of the Braves amid a Major League Baseball investigation into Atlanta\'s international signings, having committed what the Braves termed "a breach of MLB rules regarding the international player market".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On November 13, 2017, the Braves announced Alex Anthopoulos as the new general manager and executive vice president.<sup id="cite_ref-aajh_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aajh-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> John Hart was removed as team president and assumed a senior adviser role with the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-aajh_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aajh-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Braves chairman Terry McGuirk apologized to fans "on behalf of the entire Braves family" for the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-aajh_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aajh-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> McGuirk described Anthopoulos as "a man of integrity" and that "he will operate in a way that will make all of our Braves fans proud."<sup id="cite_ref-aajh_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aajh-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On November 17, 2017, the Braves announced that John Hart had stepped down as senior advisor for the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-jhsa_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jhsa-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>  Hart said in a statement that "with the hiring of Alex Anthopoulos as general manager, this organization is in great hands."<sup id="cite_ref-jhsa_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jhsa-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="MLB_investigation_and_penalties">MLB investigation and penalties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: MLB investigation and penalties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On November 21, 2017, Major League Baseball Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Rob_Manfred" title="Rob Manfred">Rob Manfred</a> announced the findings of the MLB investigation into Atlanta\'s international signings.<sup id="cite_ref-jcban_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jcban-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Manfred ruled that the Braves must forfeit 13 international prospects, including highly touted <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Maitan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kevin Maitan">Kevin Maitan</a>, an infielder from <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> who signed for $4.25 million in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-jcban_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jcban-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The team also forfeited a third-round draft pick in the 2018 draft. Former Braves general manager John Coppolella was placed on baseball\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_banned_from_Major_League_Baseball" title="List of people banned from Major League Baseball">permanently ineligible list</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jcban_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jcban-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Additionally, the Braves shall be prohibited from signing any international player for more than $10,000 during the 2019\xe2\x80\x9320 signing period and their international signing bonus pool for the 2020\xe2\x80\x9321 signing period will be reduced by 50 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-jcban_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jcban-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a full season-by-season list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Braves_seasons" title="List of Atlanta Braves seasons">List of Atlanta Braves seasons</a>.</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Series_championships">World Series championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: World Series championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Over its 138 seasons, the Braves franchise has won a total of three <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> Championships, one in each of the three cities they have played in.\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="1" border="1" cellspacing="0" style="width:60%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#16284F;color:#FFFFFF;;">Season\n</th>\n<th Score\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#16284F;color:#FFFFFF;;">Record\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/1914_World_Series" title="1914 World Series">1914</a> championships:</b>\n</td>\n<td><span style="color:#fff;"><b>3</b>\n</span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_rivalries">Major rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Major rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Mets">New York Mets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: New York Mets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Braves%E2%80%93Mets_rivalry" title="Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry">Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry is a rivalry between the two teams, featuring the Braves and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> as they both play in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RivalryWithMets_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RivalryWithMets-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although their first major confrontation occurred when the Mets swept the Braves in the <a href="/wiki/1969_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1969 National League Championship Series">1969 NLCS</a>, en route to their first World Series championship, the first playoff series won by an expansion team (also the first playoff appearance by an expansion team), the rivalry did not become especially heated until the 1994 season when division realignment put both the Mets and the Braves in the NL East division.<sup id="cite_ref-Realignment_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Realignment-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> During this time the Braves became one of the most dominant teams in professional baseball, earning 14 straight division titles through 2005, including five world series berths, and one world series championship during the 1995 season. The rivalry remained heated through the early 2000s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philadelphia_Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Philadelphia Phillies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>While their rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> lacks the history and hatred of the Mets, it has been the more important one in the last decade. Between 1993 and 2013, the two teams reigned almost exclusively as NL East champions, the exceptions being in 2006, when the Mets won their first division title since <a href="/wiki/1988_New_York_Mets_season" title="1988 New York Mets season">1988</a> (no division titles were awarded in 1994 due to the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">player\'s strike</a>), and in 2012, when the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> claimed their <a href="/wiki/National_League_East#NL_East_champions_by_year" title="National League East">first division title since 1981</a> when playing as the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>. The Phillies 1993 championship was also part of a four-year reign of exclusive division championships by the Phillies and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, their <a href="/wiki/Phillies%E2%80%93Pirates_rivalry" title="Phillies\xe2\x80\x93Pirates rivalry">in-state rivals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> While rivalries are generally characterized by mutual hatred, the Braves and Phillies deeply respect each other. Each game played (18 games in 2011) is vastly important between these two NL East giants, but at the end of the day, they are very similar organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>  Overall, the Braves have one more <a href="/wiki/National_League_East#Most_Division_Titles" title="National League East">National League East division title</a> than the Phillies, having won 12 times each since 1969, with the Braves holding it for eleven consecutive years from 1995 through 2005.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-style:bold; border:3px;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/File:MPrado01.jpg" class="image" title="Mart\xc3\xadn Prado wearing the home uniform"><img alt="Mart\xc3\xadn Prado wearing the home uniform" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="512" /></a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/File:MG_9800_Ben_Sheets.jpg" class="image" title="Ben Sheets wearing the away uniform"><img alt="Ben Sheets wearing the /></a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/File:Gregor_Blanco.jpg" class="image" title="Gregor Blanco wearing the second alternate home uniform"><img alt="Gregor Blanco wearing the second alternate home data-file-height="333" /></a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Bourn_on_April_5,_2012.jpg" class="image" title="Michael Bourn wearing the alternate away uniform"><img alt="Michael Bourn wearing the alternate away uniform" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg/110px-Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg" width="110" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg/165px-Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Michael_Bourn_on_April_5%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="1520" /></a>\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<p>The Braves currently have five different game <a href="/wiki/Baseball_uniform" title="Baseball uniform">baseball uniform</a> combinations. The home uniforms consist of a standard white uniform, a red, military appreciation jersey worn with the standard white pants, and a cream alternate uniform. The road uniforms consist of a standard gray uniform, and an alternate navy blue jersey worn with the standard gray pants.\n</p><p>The white home uniform, introduced in 1987, is the primary home uniform. The jersey has "Braves" written in script across the chest with the tomahawk logo underneath. The jersey also includes piping around the collar and down the front of the jersey and around the bottom of the sleeves. Player numbers appear on the back of the jersey with a nameplate above. The Braves script, player numbers, and piping are red with a navy blue border. The tomahawk is primarily red with blue and yellow detail and a navy blue border. The white pants have identical piping to the jersey about the belt loops and down the outside seam of the pants. The player names consist of navy blue lettering sewn to a white nameplate. The player names originally used vertically arched lettering but, since 2006, the team has used radially arched lettering. The white uniform is paired with the standard home cap. It is a red brimmed, navy blue cap with a white embroidered "script A" logo. The home batting helmet is identical to the primary home cap.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The gray road uniforms are the primary road uniform. The uniforms are identical to the white home uniforms with the exception of the "Braves" script, which is replaced by the "Atlanta" script. Player names are sewn to a gray nameplate. The primary uniforms are very similar to the uniforms that the Braves wore from 1946 to 1965\xe2\x80\x94during their latter years in Boston and throughout their tenure in Milwaukee.\n</p><p>The red, military appreciation jersey was introduced on February 5, 2014. The jerseys feature navy blue piping with a white border, the Braves script in blue with white stars, and the American Flag on the left sleeve. The updated red jerseys will not include the tomahawk logo. The jerseys will be worn for five home games in 2014: April 26 vs. the Cincinnati Reds (military family night), June 13 vs. the LA Angels of Anaheim (celebrating the Army), July 26 vs. the San Diego Padres (celebrating the Marines), Aug. 30 vs. the Miami Marlins (celebrating the Navy), and September 19 vs. NY Mets (celebrating the Air Force).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  The jerseys will be paired with camouflage caps.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>  The military appreciation jerseys replace the red jerseys introduced in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>  Worn with the white pants, these jerseys included the same elements as the white jerseys, with the Braves script, player numbers, and piping in navy blue with a white border. The tomahawk was primarily blue, with red and yellow detail and a white border. The player names consisted of white lettering sewn to a red nameplate. These jerseys were paired with an alternate home cap, which was a red brimmed, navy blue cap with a red, embroidered "script A" logo with a tomahawk, outlined in white. The alternate cap did not have a matching batting helmet. The red alternate jerseys were worn for Sunday home games from 2005 to 2011. The only exceptions to this were the opening game of the 2005 <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">NLDS</a>, which was played on a Wednesday, and on Memorial Day in 2006. The 2006 Memorial Day game is also the only time the red jerseys were paired with the primary home cap. With the introduction of the cream uniform in 2012, the red jerseys were worn for Friday night home games from 2012 to 2013. However, the Braves chose to wear the traditional white jerseys for their 2012 home opener, which took place on Friday, April 13.\n</p><p>The cream alternate uniforms were introduced in February 2012 as a tribute to the Braves\' first season in Atlanta in 1966. The jersey includes the "Braves" script across the breastplate, but the player number replaces the tomahawk underneath the "Braves" script on the left placket. Player numbers and the "Braves" script are in red with a navy blue border. The player names consist of navy blue lettering sewn to a cream nameplate. The jersey has a thin, navy piping about the collar and down the front of the jersey. There is no piping around the sleeves. The cream pants include piping identical to the jersey down the outside seam. The left sleeve of the jersey has a "crossed tomahawk" logo that replaces the "screaming Indian" logo that appeared on the 1966 jerseys. The new logo has two, primarily red, crossed tomahawks. Underneath the tomahawks is a blue circle outlined in red, with "1876" in red above (commemorating the year the franchise was founded), and "Atlanta Braves" in white below. The cream uniforms are paired with the standard home cap and are worn for Saturday and Sunday home games.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The alternate navy blue road jerseys were introduced on opening night of the 2008 season against the Washington Nationals. Worn with the gray road pants, the jerseys feature the "Atlanta" script on the breastplate in navy blue with a white outline. The tomahawk is primarily navy blue with red and yellow detail and a white border. The player numbers are blue with white borders and the player names are white letters sewn to a navy blue nameplate. The navy blue jerseys have no piping either on the sleeves or around the collar.\n</p><p>From 1987 to 2008, the red brimmed, primary home cap was also worn on the road. However, when the navy blue jerseys were introduced in 2008, they were paired with a navy blue cap, similar to the team\'s road cap worn from 1966 to 1971. While the red brimmed cap was still primarily worn with the gray road uniforms, the team sometimes wore the navy blue cap with the gray jerseys, and the red brimmed cap was occasionally worn with the navy blue jerseys. The red brimmed home batting helmets were also worn on the road from 1987 through 2008. Beginning in 2009, the navy blue cap became the official road cap and was paired with a navy blue road batting helmet.\n</p><p>Unlike the home uniforms, which are worn based on a schedule, the road uniforms are chosen on game day by the starting pitcher. However, they are also subject to <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> rules requiring the road team to wear uniforms that contrast with the uniforms worn by the home team. Due to this rule, the gray uniforms are worn when the home team chooses to wear navy blue, and sometimes when the home team chooses to wear black.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos">Logos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Logos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Native_American_mascot_controversy#Atlanta_Braves" title="Native American mascot controversy">Native American, Atlanta Braves logo information</a></div>\n<p>From 1945 to 1955 the Braves primary logo consisted of the head of an Indian warrior.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> From 1956 to 1965 it was a laughing Indian with a mohawk and one feather in his hair.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> When the Braves moved to Atlanta in 1966, the "Braves" script was added underneath the laughing Indian.<sup id="cite_ref-alogo_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alogo-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 1985, the Braves made a small script change to the logo.<sup id="cite_ref-alogo_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alogo-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The Braves modern logo debuted in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-alogo_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alogo-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The modern logo is the word "Braves" in cursive with a tomahawk below it.<sup id="cite_ref-alogo_86-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alogo-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the Braves made a subtle color change to the primary logo.<sup id="cite_ref-alogo_86-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alogo-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="Atlanta Braves award winners and league leaders">Atlanta Braves award winners and league leaders</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_records">Team records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Team records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Braves_team_records" title="List of Atlanta Braves team records">List of Atlanta Braves team Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>\'s 44, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Murphy" title="Dale Murphy">Dale Murphy</a>\'s 3, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Niekro" title="Phil Niekro">Phil Niekro</a>\'s 35, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Mathews" title="Eddie Mathews">Eddie Mathews</a>\' 41, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Spahn" title="Warren Spahn">Warren Spahn</a>\'s 21 and <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s 42, which is retired for all of baseball with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson_Day" title="Jackie Robinson Day">Jackie Robinson Day</a>, have also been retired.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The color and design of the retired numbers reflect the uniform design at the time the person was on the team, excluding Robinson.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table id="SunTrust_Park">SunTrust Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: SunTrust Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n<table style="width:300px; font-size:90%; border:1px solid #CE1F43;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center; font-size:larger;">\n<td colspan="6" style="background-color:#16284F;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>Home Attendance at SunTrust Park</b><sup id="cite_ref-att_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-att-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><b></b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background-color:#CE1F43;color:#FFFFFF;;">\n<td><b>Year</b></td>\n<td><b>Total Attendance</b></td>\n<td><b>Game Average</b></td>\n<td><b>Stadium Capacity by&#160;%</b></td>\n<td><b>Major League Rank by #</b></td>\n<td><b> Major League Rank by&#160;%</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2017_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2017 Atlanta Braves season">2017</a>\n</td>\n<td>2,505,252\n</td>\n<td>30,929\n</td>\n<td>75.3%\n</td>\n<td>13th\n</td>\n<td>10th\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Braves_broadcasters" title="List of Atlanta Braves broadcasters">List of Atlanta Braves broadcasters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braves_TBS_Baseball" title="Braves TBS Baseball">Braves TBS Baseball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves_Radio_Network" title="Atlanta Braves Radio Network">Atlanta Braves Radio Network</a></div>\n<p>After years of stability, the Braves have faced a period of transition in their radio and television coverage.\n</p><p>The 2007 season was the last for Braves baseball on the <a href="/wiki/TBS_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (TV network)">TBS Superstation</a>. TBS showed 70 games throughout the country, then cleared the decks to make way for a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_TBS" title="Major League Baseball on TBS">new national broadcast package</a> that began in earnest with the 2007 postseason, and expanded to Sunday afternoon games in 2008. Until his dismissal in 2009, <a href="/wiki/Chip_Caray" title="Chip Caray">Chip Caray</a>, one of the Braves\' current broadcasters, called <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> for the national package, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Division_Series" title="Division Series">Division Series</a> every season and alternating coverage of the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">NLCS</a>. Caray is joined by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Simpson_(baseball)" title="Joe Simpson (baseball)">Joe Simpson</a>, who has provided color commentary for the Braves since 1992.\n</p><p>Braves baseball had been on TBS since it was WTCG in 1972 and had been a cornerstone of the national superstation since it began in 1976. <a href="/wiki/WPCH-TV" title="WPCH-TV">WPCH-TV/Peachtree TV</a>, formerly WTBS Atlanta, still carried Braves games after 2007, but only in parts of the Southern United States. After the transfer of the channel\'s operations from Time Warner to <a href="/wiki/Meredith_Corporation" title="Meredith Corporation">Meredith Corporation</a>, all Peachtree TV games were simulcast on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_South" title="Fox Sports South">Fox Sports South</a> outside of the Peachtree TV coverage area in 2011 and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  On February 27, 2013, it was announced that Fox Sports South and SportSouth (now called <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Southeast" title="Fox Sports Southeast">Fox Sports Southeast</a>) would carry every regionally televised Braves game exclusively, ending the team\'s partnership with WPCH-TV after 40 years.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the 2004 season, longtime radio flagship station <a href="/wiki/WSB_(AM)" title="WSB (AM)">750 WSB</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/WGST" title="WGST">WGST</a> 640AM. Due to WGST\'s weak signal at night, which fails to cover the entire <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_metropolitan_area" title="Atlanta metropolitan area">Atlanta metropolitan area</a>, all games began to be simulcast on <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="FM radio">FM radio</a> when the rights were transferred. The games first appeared on 96.1 <a href="/wiki/WWPW" title="WWPW">WKLS</a> (formerly "96 Rock") in 2005, but moved to <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a> station 94.9 <a href="/wiki/WUBL" title="WUBL">WUBL</a> ("94.9 The Bull") in 2007 after WKLS underwent a change in format from <a href="/wiki/Classic_rock" title="Classic rock">classic rock</a> to <a href="/wiki/Active_rock" title="Active rock">active rock</a> and became <a href="/wiki/WWPW" title="WWPW">Project 9\xe2\x80\x936\xe2\x80\x931</a>. As of the 2009 season, the Braves returned to WKLS on the FM frequency but remained on WGST on AM. It was announced that for the 2010 season, the Braves will be flagshipped on <a href="/wiki/WCNN" title="WCNN">WCNN</a> 680 The Fan and in Atlanta on the AM dial and <a href="/wiki/WNNX" title="WNNX">WNNX</a> 100.5 FM.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Atlanta Braves radio network currently serves 134 radio stations across the Southern United States, including 20 in <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, 4 in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, 68 in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, 1 in <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, 13 in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, 14 in <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, and 14 in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2009, the radio announcers have been former Brewers announcer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Powell_(sportscaster)" title="Jim Powell (sportscaster)">Jim Powell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Sutton" title="Don Sutton">Don Sutton</a>. Sutton was released after the <a href="/wiki/2006_in_baseball" title="2006 in baseball">2006 season</a> and called <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> games on television from 2007 to 2008, but he has since returned for the 2009 season.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Longtime Braves voices <a href="/wiki/Skip_Caray" title="Skip Caray">Skip Caray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Van_Wieren" title="Pete Van Wieren">Pete Van Wieren</a> were the primary play-by-play voices of Braves baseball until Skip\'s sudden death on August 3, 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and Van Wieren\'s retirement after the 2008 season.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The team\'s official colors are navy blue and scarlet red, according to the team\'s mascot (BLOOPER)\'s official website.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a founded in 1871. The Braves have played more consecutive seasons.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_Braves&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Citations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mlb.com/braves/fans/entertainment-teams/blooper">"Meet BLOOPER"</a>. <i>Braves.com</i>. <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.
